Question 1medium

India's Five Year Plans were a feature of which economic model?

  1. Socialist/Mixed economy planning — Soviet-influenced centralized planning to guide economic development (1951-2017)
  2. Pure capitalist economy
  3. Free market economy
  4. Laissez-faire economy
Show answer

Answer: Socialist/Mixed economy planning — Soviet-influenced centralized planning to guide economic development (1951-2017)

India's Five-Year Plans (1951-2017, 12 plans total) were inspired by Soviet Union's central planning model. First Plan (1951-56): agriculture focus (Bhakra dam, community development). Second Plan (Nehru-Mahalanobis): heavy industry. 12th Plan ended 2017. NITI Aayog replaced with strategy documents.

Question 2medium

The First Five Year Plan of India (1951-56) focused on:

  1. Agriculture, irrigation, and power (dams: Bhakra-Nangal, Hirakud, Damodar Valley); based on Harrod-Domar growth model
  2. Heavy industrialization
  3. IT sector
  4. Infrastructure only
Show answer

Answer: Agriculture, irrigation, and power (dams: Bhakra-Nangal, Hirakud, Damodar Valley); based on Harrod-Domar growth model

First FYP (1951-56): priority on agriculture, irrigation, and power generation to overcome food shortages and post-partition economic disruption. Planned outlay: Rs 2,069 crore. Major projects: Bhakra-Nangal (Punjab), Damodar Valley Corporation, Hirakud Dam. Also focused on land reforms.

Question 3easy

Public Distribution System (PDS) in India is meant to:

  1. Distribute subsidized food grains (rice, wheat, sugar, kerosene) to Below Poverty Line (BPL) families through ration shops (Fair Price Shops)
  2. Distribute fertilizers
  3. Manage mid-day meals in schools
  4. Export food grains
Show answer

Answer: Distribute subsidized food grains (rice, wheat, sugar, kerosene) to Below Poverty Line (BPL) families through ration shops (Fair Price Shops)

PDS: network of about 5.3 lakh Fair Price Shops (ration shops) distributing subsidized food. Managed jointly by central (Food Corporation of India procures and allocates) and state governments (distributes). NFSA 2013 (National Food Security Act) extended PDS to ~81 crore people (75% rural, 50% urban population).

Question 4medium

The Minimum Support Price (MSP) is:

  1. Government-guaranteed price for agricultural produce — ensures farmers get fair price and are not exploited by market forces; recommended by CACP
  2. Market price of commodities
  3. Minimum wage for agricultural workers
  4. Tax on agricultural income
Show answer

Answer: Government-guaranteed price for agricultural produce — ensures farmers get fair price and are not exploited by market forces; recommended by CACP

MSP: announced by Central Government (based on CACP — Commission for Agricultural Costs and Prices recommendations) before sowing season. Government agencies (FCI, NAFED) purchase crops at MSP if market price falls below it. MSP for 23 major crops including paddy, wheat, pulses, oilseeds, and cotton. Not legally binding on private buyers.

Question 5easy

The National Rural Employment Guarantee Act (MGNREGA) guarantees:

  1. 100 days of unskilled manual work per year to any rural household that demands it — minimum wage paid, unemployed allowance if work not provided within 15 days
  2. 200 days of work
  3. Employment to urban workers
  4. Skilled employment only
Show answer

Answer: 100 days of unskilled manual work per year to any rural household that demands it — minimum wage paid, unemployed allowance if work not provided within 15 days

MGNREGA (2005, implemented 2006): provides legal right to 100 days of unskilled work per household per year at minimum wage. If work not provided within 15 days, unemployment allowance paid. Works include road construction, water conservation, land development. Among world's largest social protection programs. Renamed to include Gandhi: MGNREGS.

Question 6easy

The Pradhan Mantri Jan Dhan Yojana (PMJDY) aims at:

  1. Financial inclusion — opening zero-balance bank accounts for unbanked sections with RuPay debit card, overdraft facility, and insurance
  2. Free LPG connections
  3. Healthcare for poor
  4. Rural electrification
Show answer

Answer: Financial inclusion — opening zero-balance bank accounts for unbanked sections with RuPay debit card, overdraft facility, and insurance

PMJDY (August 28, 2014): world's largest financial inclusion initiative. Features: zero-balance savings account (Jan Dhan account), RuPay debit card with Rs 2 lakh accident insurance, Rs 30,000 life insurance, Rs 10,000 overdraft facility. By 2024: 52+ crore accounts opened, mostly in rural areas.

Question 7medium

The NABARD (National Bank for Agriculture and Rural Development) was established in:

  1. 1982 — apex bank for agricultural and rural credit; provides refinance to cooperative banks, RRBs, and commercial banks for agricultural loans
  2. 1935
  3. 1969
  4. 2000
Show answer

Answer: 1982 — apex bank for agricultural and rural credit; provides refinance to cooperative banks, RRBs, and commercial banks for agricultural loans

NABARD (est. July 12, 1982) based on B. Sivaraman Committee recommendations. HQ: Mumbai. Functions: refinancing apex cooperative banks, RRBs (Regional Rural Banks), and commercial banks for agriculture/rural development; rural infrastructure development (RIDF); watershed development; Self-Help Group (SHG) - Bank Linkage Programme.

Question 8easy

The Pradhan Mantri Awas Yojana (PMAY) aims to provide:

  1. Housing for All — affordable housing to urban and rural poor by 2022 (extended to 2024); includes PMAY-Urban and PMAY-Gramin
  2. Free food for all
  3. Employment guarantee
  4. Healthcare for all
Show answer

Answer: Housing for All — affordable housing to urban and rural poor by 2022 (extended to 2024); includes PMAY-Urban and PMAY-Gramin

PMAY (2015): targets housing for all urban slum dwellers and rural homeless. PMAY-Urban: credit-linked subsidy scheme for home loans (for EWS/LIG/MIG). PMAY-Gramin: provides Rs 1.2 lakh (plain areas) or Rs 1.3 lakh (NE, hilly) grant for rural house construction. Completed 3 crore+ houses.

Question 9hard

The term 'poverty line' in India is determined by:

  1. Minimum monthly per capita expenditure needed to meet basic food, clothing, and shelter needs — currently based on Tendulkar Committee methodology (modified by Rangarajan Committee)
  2. Annual income below Rs 1 lakh
  3. BPL card possession
  4. Urban/rural classification only
Show answer

Answer: Minimum monthly per capita expenditure needed to meet basic food, clothing, and shelter needs — currently based on Tendulkar Committee methodology (modified by Rangarajan Committee)

India's Poverty Line: Tendulkar Committee (2009): Rs 816/month urban, Rs 672/month rural (2011-12 prices). Rangarajan Committee (2014): higher threshold — Rs 1407 urban, Rs 972 rural. SECC (Socio-Economic and Caste Census) used for targeting welfare programs. About 21% of population below poverty line (World Bank $1.90/day PPP criterion).

Question 10medium

Remittances from Non-Resident Indians (NRIs) contribute to India's:

  1. Current Account (in Balance of Payments) — India is the world's largest remittance recipient (~$100 billion annually)
  2. Capital Account only
  3. Trade Balance (goods exports)
  4. Fiscal deficit
Show answer

Answer: Current Account (in Balance of Payments) — India is the world's largest remittance recipient (~$100 billion annually)

NRI remittances: India consistently receives the highest remittances globally (~$100 billion in 2022-23). Recorded under 'transfers' in the Current Account of BoP. Major sources: USA, UAE, Saudi Arabia, Kuwait, UK. They help finance India's current account deficit and support rural household incomes.

Question 11medium

The National Rural Health Mission (NHM) was launched in:

  1. 2005 — to improve healthcare in rural India; later merged with National Urban Health Mission to form NHM in 2013; ASHAs (Accredited Social Health Activists) are key workers
  2. 2000
  3. 2010
  4. 1995
Show answer

Answer: 2005 — to improve healthcare in rural India; later merged with National Urban Health Mission to form NHM in 2013; ASHAs (Accredited Social Health Activists) are key workers

NRHM (National Rural Health Mission, 2005): flagship health scheme for rural areas. Key feature: ASHA workers — trained female community health activists (one per 1000 population) who link communities with health facilities. NRHM + National Urban Health Mission merged into NHM (National Health Mission) in 2013.

Question 12medium

The Atal Innovation Mission (AIM) was established under:

  1. NITI Aayog — to promote innovation and entrepreneurship across India through Atal Tinkering Labs (ATLs) in schools and Atal Incubation Centres (AICs)
  2. Ministry of Finance
  3. CSIR
  4. RBI
Show answer

Answer: NITI Aayog — to promote innovation and entrepreneurship across India through Atal Tinkering Labs (ATLs) in schools and Atal Incubation Centres (AICs)

AIM (2016, under NITI Aayog): flagship initiative to promote innovation. Key programs: Atal Tinkering Labs (ATLs) — maker spaces in schools (Grades 6-12) with 3D printers, robotics kits, etc. Atal Incubation Centres (AICs): support startups. Atal Community Innovation Centres (ACICs): tier-2/3 cities and rural areas.

Question 13hard

The Eleventh Schedule of the Indian Constitution lists subjects under:

  1. Panchayati Raj institutions (29 subjects including agriculture, land, roads, drinking water, education, poverty alleviation) after 73rd Amendment 1992
  2. State legislature subjects
  3. Union List subjects
  4. Concurrent List subjects
Show answer

Answer: Panchayati Raj institutions (29 subjects including agriculture, land, roads, drinking water, education, poverty alleviation) after 73rd Amendment 1992

73rd Constitutional Amendment (1992): gave constitutional status to Panchayati Raj (3-tier local self-government). 11th Schedule: 29 subjects devolved to panchayats including: agriculture, land reforms, rural electrification, water management, primary education, primary health, roads, poverty alleviation. States choose which subjects to actually transfer.

Question 14easy

The Swachh Bharat Abhiyan (Clean India Mission) was launched on:

  1. October 2, 2014 (Gandhi Jayanti) — to achieve Open Defecation Free (ODF) India; 9 crore+ toilets built; PM Modi started by personally sweeping Valmiki colony, New Delhi
  2. August 15, 2014
  3. January 26, 2015
  4. April 5, 2016
Show answer

Answer: October 2, 2014 (Gandhi Jayanti) — to achieve Open Defecation Free (ODF) India; 9 crore+ toilets built; PM Modi started by personally sweeping Valmiki colony, New Delhi

Swachh Bharat Mission (Oct 2, 2014, Gandhi's 145th birthday): two sub-missions — SBM-Grameen (rural, MoDRWS) and SBM-Urban (MoHUA). Phase 1 (2014-19): ODF (Open Defecation Free) goal — 60 crore people stopped open defecation. Phase 2 (2020-25): ODF+, solid/liquid waste management, plastic waste management.

Question 15medium

The Bharat Net project aims to:

  1. Provide broadband connectivity to all Gram Panchayats (2.5 lakh panchayats) using OFC, radio, and satellite — run by BSNL/DOT; enable Digital India in rural areas
  2. Build highways
  3. Develop ports
  4. Electrify villages (that's Saubhagya scheme)
Show answer

Answer: Provide broadband connectivity to all Gram Panchayats (2.5 lakh panchayats) using OFC, radio, and satellite — run by BSNL/DOT; enable Digital India in rural areas

BharatNet (2011, earlier NOFN — National Optical Fibre Network): world's largest rural broadband connectivity project. Connects all 2.5 lakh gram panchayats with optical fiber (OFC). Implemented by BSNL through state governments. Enables: e-governance, telemedicine, e-education, e-commerce in rural India. Essential backbone for Digital India.

Question 16medium

Food Corporation of India (FCI) was established to:

  1. Procure food grains from farmers at MSP, store, and distribute them through PDS — established 1965; HQ: New Delhi; India's largest food storage network
  2. Export food grains
  3. Process food products
  4. Regulate food prices directly
Show answer

Answer: Procure food grains from farmers at MSP, store, and distribute them through PDS — established 1965; HQ: New Delhi; India's largest food storage network

FCI (1965, FCI Act 1964): functions: procurement of wheat and rice from farmers at MSP (mainly Punjab, Haryana, UP), building and managing strategic food reserves (buffer stocks), distributing to state governments for PDS at Central Issue Price (CIP). FCI's buffer stock of grain helps stabilize prices and ensure food security.

Question 17easy

The Pradhan Mantri Kaushal Vikas Yojana (PMKVY) is a scheme for:

  1. Skill development — free short-term training to youth in industry-relevant skills; recognition of prior learning (RPL); National Skill Development Corporation (NSDC) implements it
  2. Mid-day meals
  3. Employment guarantee
  4. Housing for youth
Show answer

Answer: Skill development — free short-term training to youth in industry-relevant skills; recognition of prior learning (RPL); National Skill Development Corporation (NSDC) implements it

PMKVY (2015): flagship skill development scheme under Skill India Mission. Free short-term training across 300+ job roles in 38 sectors (construction, IT, healthcare, agriculture, etc.). On successful training + assessment: placement assistance and Rs 8,000 reward. PMKVY 4.0: focus on Industry 4.0 skills, digital and green jobs.

Question 18hard

The Bharat Broadband Network Limited (BBNL) was merged with BSNL to implement:

  1. BharatNet project — providing optical fiber broadband to all gram panchayats; BBNL was Special Purpose Vehicle set up 2012; merged with BSNL 2023
  2. 4G rollout in cities
  3. Satellite internet
  4. National telecom policy
Show answer

Answer: BharatNet project — providing optical fiber broadband to all gram panchayats; BBNL was Special Purpose Vehicle set up 2012; merged with BSNL 2023

BBNL (Bharat Broadband Network Limited, 2012): Special Purpose Vehicle to implement BharatNet (initially NOFN). In 2023, government merged BBNL with BSNL to streamline the BharatNet project and leverage BSNL's existing infrastructure, workforce, and right-of-way permissions for faster rural broadband rollout.

Question 19medium

The Asian Development Bank (ADB) is headquartered in:

  1. Manila, Philippines — established 1966; provides loans/technical assistance to developing Asian countries; India is the largest borrower from ADB
  2. Tokyo
  3. Singapore
  4. Beijing
Show answer

Answer: Manila, Philippines — established 1966; provides loans/technical assistance to developing Asian countries; India is the largest borrower from ADB

ADB (Asian Development Bank, 1966): HQ in Manila, Philippines. 68 member countries (49 from Asia-Pacific). Provides: project loans, policy-based loans, technical assistance, equity investments. India is one of ADB's largest borrowers (infrastructure, urban development, agriculture). USA and Japan are largest shareholders.

Question 20easy

The Pradhan Mantri Gram Sadak Yojana (PMGSY) was launched to:

  1. Provide all-weather road connectivity to unconnected habitations (500+ population in plain areas, 250+ in hilly/tribal areas) — launched 2000, PM Atal Bihari Vajpayee
  2. Build national highways
  3. Build expressways
  4. Develop urban roads only
Show answer

Answer: Provide all-weather road connectivity to unconnected habitations (500+ population in plain areas, 250+ in hilly/tribal areas) — launched 2000, PM Atal Bihari Vajpayee

PMGSY (2000): flagship scheme to provide all-weather road connectivity to unconnected rural habitations. Target: 500+ population habitations in plain areas, 250+ in NE/hilly/tribal. World's largest rural road program. PMGSY Phase III (2019): upgrade 1.25 lakh km of existing rural roads. Funded 60% Centre: 40% State (90:10 for NE/special category).

Question 21medium

NABARD's function of refinancing is:

  1. Providing funds to cooperative banks, Regional Rural Banks (RRBs), and commercial banks against their agriculture/rural lending portfolio — enabling them to extend more credit to farmers
  2. Providing loans directly to farmers only
  3. Setting agricultural prices
  4. Managing FCI stocks
Show answer

Answer: Providing funds to cooperative banks, Regional Rural Banks (RRBs), and commercial banks against their agriculture/rural lending portfolio — enabling them to extend more credit to farmers

NABARD refinancing: Short-term credit (seasonal agricultural operations: crop loans) and Long-term credit (land development, farm machinery, irrigation) to: District/State Cooperative Banks, Regional Rural Banks, Commercial Banks. NABARD also gives direct loans to state governments (RIDF — Rural Infrastructure Development Fund) for rural projects.

Question 22hard

The Agri-Stack or Digital Agriculture Mission aims to:

  1. Create a digital public infrastructure (DPI) for agriculture — farmer registry, crop sown registry, farm boundaries using satellite/GIS to enable precision farming and targeted subsidies
  2. Replace all agricultural workers with robots
  3. Automate MSP procurement
  4. Create digital agricultural exports only
Show answer

Answer: Create a digital public infrastructure (DPI) for agriculture — farmer registry, crop sown registry, farm boundaries using satellite/GIS to enable precision farming and targeted subsidies

Digital Agriculture Mission / Agri-Stack (2021-2025): federated farmer database (Farmer ID linked to land records, Aadhaar), Crop Sown Registry (what crops are grown, digitized land records), Remote Sensing and GIS maps of farm plots. Enables: targeted input delivery (seeds, fertilizer), precision advisory (weather, crop insurance, agri-credit).

Question 23medium

The Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank (AIIB) is:

  1. Multilateral development bank proposed by China (2013), established 2015 — 106 members; HQ Beijing; funds infrastructure in Asia; India is the 2nd largest shareholder
  2. ADB branch
  3. World Bank subsidiary
  4. IMF initiative
Show answer

Answer: Multilateral development bank proposed by China (2013), established 2015 — 106 members; HQ Beijing; funds infrastructure in Asia; India is the 2nd largest shareholder

AIIB (Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank, 2015): proposed by China's Xi Jinping. 57 founding members. HQ: Beijing. Focus: infrastructure (energy, transport, urban, rural, communications) in Asia. China: largest shareholder (~26%); India: 2nd largest (~8%). The US and Japan did not join (seeing it as China's geopolitical tool). India has received several AIIB loans for transport and urban infrastructure.

Question 24hard

India's first Regional Rural Bank (RRB) was:

  1. Prathama Grameen Bank, established October 2, 1975 in Moradabad, Uttar Pradesh — sponsored by Syndicate Bank
  2. SBI Gramin Bank
  3. Syndicate Bank RRB
  4. Punjab National Bank Rural Bank
Show answer

Answer: Prathama Grameen Bank, established October 2, 1975 in Moradabad, Uttar Pradesh — sponsored by Syndicate Bank

Prathama Bank (now Prathama UP Gramin Bank after merger): first RRB established October 2, 1975, Gandhi Jayanti, in Moradabad, UP. Sponsored by Syndicate Bank. 5 RRBs simultaneously established as pilot. Based on Narasimham Committee recommendations (1975). Total 5 initial RRBs: Prathama (Moradabad), Gorakhpur Kshetriya Gramin (UP), Haryana Kshetriya Gramin (Bhiwani), Jaipur Nagaur Anchalik (Rajasthan), Singhbhum (Bihar).

Question 25hard

India's 'Silent Revolution' in agriculture refers to:

  1. Second Green Revolution for eastern India (Bihar, West Bengal, Odisha, UP) and diversification into horticulture, animal husbandry, and fisheries; also called 'Evergreen Revolution' by M.S. Swaminathan
  2. Original Green Revolution
  3. White Revolution
  4. Blue Revolution
Show answer

Answer: Second Green Revolution for eastern India (Bihar, West Bengal, Odisha, UP) and diversification into horticulture, animal husbandry, and fisheries; also called 'Evergreen Revolution' by M.S. Swaminathan

Second Green Revolution/Evergreen Revolution (M.S. Swaminathan): need to extend agricultural productivity gains to eastern India and dryland farming regions while maintaining ecological sustainability. Also: shift from cereal monoculture to diversification (horticulture, dairying, poultry, fisheries) for nutritional security and farmer income.

Question 26hard

India's 'Unified Portal for Agricultural Statistics' (UPAg) was launched to:

  1. Provide real-time agricultural data — crop sowing area, production estimates, MSP, market prices — to farmers, policymakers, and researchers via a single platform
  2. Replace FCI
  3. Automate MSP procurement
  4. Provide agri loans directly
Show answer

Answer: Provide real-time agricultural data — crop sowing area, production estimates, MSP, market prices — to farmers, policymakers, and researchers via a single platform

UPAg (2022, Ministry of Agriculture): first-of-its-kind single platform integrating agricultural statistics from multiple agencies. Data: crop sowing/area, production, trade, price (wholesale, retail, MSP), input costs, import/export. Makes data accessible to farmers via mobile app. Aims to improve crop planning and reduce information asymmetry.

Question 27easy

The term 'crop diversification' in agriculture means:

  1. Shifting from monoculture to growing multiple crops including horticulture, spices, oilseeds, pulses — reduces risk, improves nutrition, and can increase farmer income compared to wheat/rice only
  2. Growing only wheat and rice
  3. Farming in multiple countries
  4. Diversification of farm ownership
Show answer

Answer: Shifting from monoculture to growing multiple crops including horticulture, spices, oilseeds, pulses — reduces risk, improves nutrition, and can increase farmer income compared to wheat/rice only

Crop Diversification: growing a variety of crops (different from traditional cereal monoculture). Benefits: reduces market and weather risk, improves soil health, nutrition security, higher value crops (horticulture → higher income than cereals). Government promotes with MSP for pulses and oilseeds, cluster development programs, and horticulture development programs.

Question 28easy

The 'double cropping' system in agriculture refers to:

  1. Growing two crops per year on the same piece of land — kharif (June-November, monsoon crop: paddy, cotton, maize) + rabi (November-April, winter crop: wheat, mustard, chickpea)
  2. Growing crops in two countries
  3. Two varieties of same crop simultaneously
  4. Mixed cropping of two types
Show answer

Answer: Growing two crops per year on the same piece of land — kharif (June-November, monsoon crop: paddy, cotton, maize) + rabi (November-April, winter crop: wheat, mustard, chickpea)

Double Cropping: two crops sequentially in a year. India's cropping seasons: Kharif (sown with SW monsoon, harvested Oct-Nov): paddy, cotton, maize, soybean, groundnut. Rabi (sown Nov, harvested April): wheat, mustard, chickpea, barley. Zaid (short summer season, March-June): watermelon, cucumber, vegetables. Irrigation enables double/triple cropping (Punjab, Haryana, UP).

Question 29medium

The Deen Dayal Upadhyaya Grameen Kaushalya Yojana (DDU-GKY) is:

  1. Skill training and placement program for rural poor youth (15-35 years, BPL families) — provides free training in 250+ trades, placement guarantee; part of MGNREGA complementary scheme
  2. Scholarship for rural students
  3. Employment guarantee (MGNREGA is that)
  4. Urban skill development
Show answer

Answer: Skill training and placement program for rural poor youth (15-35 years, BPL families) — provides free training in 250+ trades, placement guarantee; part of MGNREGA complementary scheme

DDU-GKY (2014, renamed Aajeevika Skills/NRLM Skills): targets rural BPL youth. Free skill training, boarding, lodging during training, and placement assistance. Coverage: 15-35 years (extended to 45 for some groups). Target: place 75%+ trained youth in paid jobs. Implemented by Ministry of Rural Development through State Rural Livelihoods Missions.

Question 30medium

The National Rural Livelihoods Mission (NRLM/Aajeevika) focuses on:

  1. Organizing rural poor into Self-Help Groups (SHGs) — credit linking, livelihood promotion, skill training; targets 10 crore rural poor women in 600 districts; launched 2011
  2. Only individual farmers
  3. Only agricultural credit
  4. Only employment guarantee (MGNREGA does that)
Show answer

Answer: Organizing rural poor into Self-Help Groups (SHGs) — credit linking, livelihood promotion, skill training; targets 10 crore rural poor women in 600 districts; launched 2011

NRLM (2011, renamed Aajeevika, now renamed DAY-NRLM — Deendayal Antyodaya Yojana): world's largest poverty alleviation program. Promotes SHGs (12-20 women) → federations (village organization) → cluster level federations → block/district level federations. Provides: bank credit linkage (SHG-BLP), livelihood promotion, skill training, financial literacy.

Question 31hard

The Pradhan Mantri Annadata Aay Sanrakshan Abhiyan (PM-AASHA) scheme comprises:

  1. Three sub-schemes: Price Support Scheme (PSS), Price Deficiency Payment Scheme (PDPS), and Private Procurement & Stockist Scheme (PPSS) — to ensure farmers get MSP even in market
  2. Only MSP announcement
  3. Only crop insurance
  4. Only direct income support
Show answer

Answer: Three sub-schemes: Price Support Scheme (PSS), Price Deficiency Payment Scheme (PDPS), and Private Procurement & Stockist Scheme (PPSS) — to ensure farmers get MSP even in market

PM-AASHA (2018): umbrella scheme for MSP implementation. PSS: government agencies physically procure crops when prices fall below MSP (for oilseeds, pulses, copra). PDPS: farmers sell in market, government pays difference between MSP and market price directly (for oilseeds). PPSS: private traders can also procure at MSP after paying security deposit (pilot for oilseeds).

Question 32medium

The 'Lead Bank Scheme' in India was launched to:

  1. Assign one bank as 'lead bank' for each district — responsible for coordinating credit plans, financial inclusion, and SHG promotion in that district; launched 1969 on Narashimham Committee recommendation
  2. Provide leadership training to bankers
  3. Make one bank responsible for all banking in a district
  4. Replace cooperative banks
Show answer

Answer: Assign one bank as 'lead bank' for each district — responsible for coordinating credit plans, financial inclusion, and SHG promotion in that district; launched 1969 on Narashimham Committee recommendation

Lead Bank Scheme (1969): one bank (public sector) designated as lead bank per district (covering all talukas). Functions: preparing annual credit plan (ACP) for the district, coordinating with other banks, promoting financial inclusion, leading SLBC (State Level Bankers' Committee) work in the district. Essential for priority sector credit planning and rural financial inclusion.

Question 33hard

India's Agriculture Export Policy 2018 targets:

  1. $60 billion agricultural exports by 2022 (now extended to 2025) from ~$30 billion baseline — through cluster-based approach, value addition, brand building (GI tags), and export infrastructure
  2. Only rice exports
  3. Only organic farming exports
  4. Import substitution
Show answer

Answer: $60 billion agricultural exports by 2022 (now extended to 2025) from ~$30 billion baseline — through cluster-based approach, value addition, brand building (GI tags), and export infrastructure

Agriculture Export Policy 2018 (Ministry of Commerce): targets doubling agri exports. Key features: Agri Export Zones (AEZ) concept, cluster-based approach (integrated 12 clusters initially), GI (Geographical Indication) products promotion (Darjeeling tea, Basmati rice, Alphonso mango), value addition promotion, infrastructure (cold chain, testing labs), e-commerce for agri exports.

Question 34medium

The concept of 'mixed economy' in India post-1991 means:

  1. Market forces determine most resource allocation; government intervenes in: externalities, public goods, infrastructure, strategic sectors, social sector — less government control than pre-1991 but more than pure laissez-faire
  2. Pure market economy
  3. Pure socialist planned economy
  4. Government controlling all prices
Show answer

Answer: Market forces determine most resource allocation; government intervenes in: externalities, public goods, infrastructure, strategic sectors, social sector — less government control than pre-1991 but more than pure laissez-faire

Post-1991 India: hybrid economy — most industries open to private sector with market-based pricing, but government retains: defence production (DRDO, HAL), atomic energy, nuclear power, railways (mostly), strategic minerals, coal. Also intervenes: agricultural prices (MSP), petroleum prices (partially regulated), utilities (electricity distribution tariff regulation), social sector (healthcare, education). 'Market-friendly' rather than 'market-only.'

Question 35easy

The Green Revolution (1960s-70s) was associated with:

  1. Norman Borlaug (Nobel Peace Prize 1970) — developed semi-dwarf HYV wheat varieties; worked with CIMMYT; brought to India by M.S. Swaminathan and promoted by PM Indira Gandhi's government
  2. Jawaharlal Nehru only
  3. Planning Commission alone
  4. NABARD's initiative
Show answer

Answer: Norman Borlaug (Nobel Peace Prize 1970) — developed semi-dwarf HYV wheat varieties; worked with CIMMYT; brought to India by M.S. Swaminathan and promoted by PM Indira Gandhi's government

Green Revolution: Norman Borlaug (USA, Nobel 1970) developed semi-dwarf wheat varieties (higher yield, resistant to lodging — bending with wind). Introduced to India by M.S. Swaminathan (who worked with IARI) under Agriculture Minister C. Subramaniam and PM Indira Gandhi's government. Punjab/Haryana became wheat-surplus states. Pakistan, Mexico also benefited. Also: IR-8 'miracle rice' (IRRI, Philippines).

Question 36medium

Priority Sector Lending (PSL) requires Indian commercial banks to lend what percentage of ANBC to priority sectors?

  1. 25%
  2. 30%
  3. 40%
  4. 50%
Show answer

Answer: 40%

PSL target: 40% of Adjusted Net Bank Credit (ANBC) for domestic scheduled commercial banks. Priority sectors: Agriculture (18%), MSMEs, Education, Housing, Weaker Sections (10%).

Question 37medium

The Periodic Labour Force Survey (PLFS) in India is conducted by:

  1. NITI Aayog
  2. Ministry of Labour
  3. National Statistical Office (NSO)
  4. NSSO under MOSPI
Show answer

Answer: National Statistical Office (NSO)

PLFS is conducted by NSO (National Statistical Office) under MoSPI. Launched 2017-18, provides quarterly urban + annual rural employment/unemployment estimates.

Question 38medium

The Agriculture Produce Market Committee (APMC) Act was designed to:

  1. Export agricultural produce
  2. Protect farmers by regulating markets and preventing exploitation by middlemen
  3. Provide crop insurance
  4. Promote organic farming
Show answer

Answer: Protect farmers by regulating markets and preventing exploitation by middlemen

APMC Acts (state subject) created regulated mandis to ensure fair prices for farmers. Critics say they create cartels. The three Farm Acts 2020 (later repealed) aimed to allow sales outside APMCs.

Question 39medium

e-NAM (electronic National Agriculture Market) is a pan-India online trading platform launched in:

  1. 2013
  2. 2016
  3. 2018
  4. 2020
Show answer

Answer: 2016

e-NAM launched April 14, 2016 by SFAC (Small Farmers Agribusiness Consortium) under Ministry of Agriculture. Connects APMC mandis online for transparent price discovery.

Question 40medium

NABARD's Rural Infrastructure Development Fund (RIDF) provides loans to:

  1. Farmers directly for crop loans
  2. State governments for rural infrastructure projects
  3. Commercial banks for priority sector shortfall
  4. Microfinance institutions
Show answer

Answer: State governments for rural infrastructure projects

RIDF: state governments and state-owned corporations borrow from NABARD to build rural infrastructure (roads, bridges, irrigation). Funded by shortfall in banks' PSL targets.

Question 41medium

A price floor is effective (binding) only when it is set:

  1. Below the equilibrium price
  2. At the equilibrium price
  3. Above the equilibrium price
  4. At zero
Show answer

Answer: Above the equilibrium price

Price floor (minimum price) is binding only above equilibrium price, creating a surplus (supply > demand). E.g., MSP set above market price creates surplus procurement. Below equilibrium = non-binding.

Question 42medium

The National Food Security Act (NFSA) 2013 provides subsidized food grains to what percentage of India's population?

  1. 50%
  2. 67%
  3. 75%
  4. 81%
Show answer

Answer: 67%

NFSA 2013: covers up to 75% rural + 50% urban population = ~67% of total population (~81.35 crore people). Provides 5 kg/person/month at subsidized rates: Rice Rs 3, Wheat Rs 2, Coarse grains Rs 1/kg.

Question 43medium

Disguised unemployment is most commonly found in:

  1. Agricultural sector — more workers than needed; marginal productivity of labor is zero; removing them does not reduce output
  2. Manufacturing sector
  3. Services sector
  4. Government sector
Show answer

Answer: Agricultural sector — more workers than needed; marginal productivity of labor is zero; removing them does not reduce output

Disguised (concealed) unemployment: more people employed than necessary; additional workers add nothing to output (zero marginal product). Common in Indian agriculture (joint farming by family members). Unlike open unemployment (person seeks work but can't find it), disguised unemployment involves apparently 'working' people.

Question 44hard

India's agricultural marketing is regulated through:

  1. State-level APMC (Agricultural Produce Market Committee) Acts — mandated that farmers sell through regulated mandis; APMC reforms (Model APMC Act 2003) and Farm Laws 2020 (repealed 2021) aimed to allow direct selling
  2. Central government alone
  3. RBI
  4. NABARD directly
Show answer

Answer: State-level APMC (Agricultural Produce Market Committee) Acts — mandated that farmers sell through regulated mandis; APMC reforms (Model APMC Act 2003) and Farm Laws 2020 (repealed 2021) aimed to allow direct selling

APMC (Agricultural Produce Market Committee) system: most states have APMCs that regulate agricultural markets (mandis). Farmers had to sell produce only through licensed commission agents in regulated markets. Critiqued for middleman exploitation. Model APMC Act 2003: allow private markets, direct farmer-buyer links. Farm Laws 2020 (allowing direct selling, contract farming) were repealed November 2021 after farmer protests.

Question 45medium

The NITI Aayog's 'Aspirational Districts Programme' targets:

  1. 112 most underdeveloped districts (selected based on composite index of health, nutrition, education, agriculture, financial inclusion, infrastructure, skill development) to rapidly improve outcomes
  2. All 740 districts
  3. Only tribal districts
  4. Only Northeast districts
Show answer

Answer: 112 most underdeveloped districts (selected based on composite index of health, nutrition, education, agriculture, financial inclusion, infrastructure, skill development) to rapidly improve outcomes

Aspirational Districts Programme (2018): 112 districts ranked on 49 indicators across 5 themes: Health & Nutrition, Education, Agriculture & Water Resources, Financial Inclusion & Skill Development, Basic Infrastructure. Real-time monitoring on Championing Change portal. 'Competitive and cooperative federalism' — districts compete and learn from each other. Success: significant improvement in health, nutrition, education indicators.

Question 53easy

  1. Covers only commercial cash crops
  2. Is mandatory for all farmers irrespective of credit status
  3. Uses technology for yield estimation and caps premium paid by farmers
  4. Is implemented exclusively by private insurance companies
Show answer

Answer: Uses technology for yield estimation and caps premium paid by farmers

PMFBY uses remote sensing, drones, and smartphones for accurate crop cutting experiments, and caps farmer premium at 2% (Kharif) and 1.5% (Rabi) of sum insured.

Question 57easy

Which of the following best describes the impact of a 'Minimum Support Price' (MSP) on the market equilibrium of a specific crop in India?

  3. It acts as a price ceiling to protect consumers from inflation.
  4. It eliminates the need for government procurement operations.

MSP acts as a price floor; when set above market equilibrium, it encourages overproduction, leading to surpluses.

Question 64easy

Question 65easy

Which of the following best describes the 'Cobweb Phenomenon' in agricultural economics?

  1. The gradual transition from traditional farming to organic farming.
  2. Price fluctuations caused by a lag between the production decision and the actual harvest.
  3. The process of land consolidation to increase the size of holdings.
  4. The impact of global trade barriers on the export of cereals.
Show answer

Answer: Price fluctuations caused by a lag between the production decision and the actual harvest.

The Cobweb model explains price volatility where producers base current production on previous prices, causing cycles of surplus and shortage.

Show answer

Diversification reduces the risk of total crop failure and prevents soil nutrient depletion caused by monocropping.

Question 112easy

Deteriorating terms of trade occur when the relative price of agricultural outputs falls compared to the industrial inputs farmers must buy.

Question 161easy

  1. A. Revenue deficit
  2. B. Fiscal deficit
  3. C. Primary deficit
  4. D. Budget deficit
Show answer

Answer: B. Fiscal deficit

Fiscal deficit indicates total borrowing needs and reflects overall government spending, including agricultural subsidies, relative to revenue.

Question 162easy

How do sterilized intervention by RBI affect agricultural credit in the economy?

  1. A. It directly increases credit flow to farmers by reducing repo rate
  2. B. It absorbs surplus liquidity without changing monetary transmission to agriculture
  3. C. It reduces CRR to encourage bank lending to agriculture
  4. D. It increases food grain procurement by public agencies
Show answer

Answer: B. It absorbs surplus liquidity without changing monetary transmission to agriculture

Sterilized interventions absorb excess liquidity without altering the monetary transmission mechanism affecting agricultural credit.

Question 163easy

What is the relationship between food grain inflation and overall CPI inflation in India?

  1. A. Food grain inflation always exceeds overall CPI inflation
  2. B. Food grain inflation is a component of CPI and significantly influences overall inflation
  3. C. Food grain inflation is completely independent of CPI inflation
  4. D. Food grain inflation is calculated separately and not included in CPI
Show answer

Answer: B. Food grain inflation is a component of CPI and significantly influences overall inflation

Food grains form an important basket component of CPI, so their inflation rate significantly affects the overall CPI inflation trajectory.

Question 164easy

Which balance of payment component is most affected by agricultural trade transactions?

  1. A. Current account deficit
  2. B. Capital account surplus
  3. C. Financial account deficit
  4. D. Reserve balance
Show answer

Answer: A. Current account deficit

Agricultural exports and imports directly impact the current account, particularly the trade balance component.

Question 165easy

  1. A. It increases information asymmetry among traders
  2. B. It creates uniform price structure across markets through technology integration
  3. C. It reduces government intervention in price determination
  4. D. It eliminates the need for agricultural reforms
Show answer

Answer: B. It creates uniform price structure across markets through technology integration

NAM aims to integrate agricultural markets through technology, enabling farmers to access uniform prices across locations.

Loan waivers involve significant government expenditure, creating fiscal pressure while addressing farmer welfare concerns.

Question 169easy

  2. B. They improve the current account by earning foreign exchange through exports
  3. C. They have no impact on balance of payments as trade is neutral
  4. D. They increase capital flight through repatriation of profits
Show answer

Answer: B. They improve the current account by earning foreign exchange through exports

Export promotion schemes increase agricultural exports, earning foreign exchange and improving the current account balance.

Question 170easy

How does a depreciation of the Indian rupee affect the trade balance of agricultural commodities?

  1. Improves export competitiveness and worsens import bill
  2. Improves import competitiveness and worsens export earnings
  3. Reduces both export and import values proportionally
  4. Has no effect on trade balance
Show answer

Answer: Improves export competitiveness and worsens import bill

Depreciation makes exports cheaper abroad, boosting exports, while raising import costs, worsening the import bill.

Question 171easy

  1. Consumer Price Index (CPI)
  2. Wholesale Price Index (WPI)
  3. Minimum Support Price (MSP)
  4. Fiscal Deficit
Show answer

Answer: Minimum Support Price (MSP)

MSP is the price at which the government procures crops, indicating its support level.

Question 172easy

What is the primary effect of a sterilized open market operation by the RBI on market liquidity?

  1. Increase in bank reserves
  2. Decrease in repo rate
  3. Contraction of liquidity without altering reserve ratios
  4. Direct increase in agricultural credit flow
Show answer

Answer: Contraction of liquidity without altering reserve ratios

Sterilization absorbs excess liquidity while keeping reserve ratios unchanged, thereby tightening market liquidity.

Question 183medium

How does the 'Green Box' subsidy under the WTO Agreement on Agriculture differ from 'Amber Box' subsidies?

  1. Green Box subsidies are trade-distorting and subject to strict reduction limits
  2. Amber Box subsidies are considered non-trade distorting and are permitted without limits
  3. Green Box subsidies include research and environmental protection, while Amber Box includes price supports
  4. Amber Box subsidies are provided only to developed nations, while Green Box are for developing nations
Show answer

Answer: Green Box subsidies include research and environmental protection, while Amber Box includes price supports

Green Box subsidies are non-distorting (e.g., R&D), while Amber Box subsidies (e.g., MSP) distort trade.

Question 191medium

What is the primary objective of the 'Price Deficiency Payment' (PDP) system used in some Indian states?

  3. To subsidize the cost of seeds and fertilizers for marginal farmers
  4. To provide insurance coverage for crop failure due to natural calamities

Question 206medium

In the context of Indian agriculture, the 'cobweb phenomenon' refers to:

  1. The cyclical fluctuation of prices due to time lags between production decisions and harvest
  2. The entanglement of farmers in multiple informal debt traps
  3. The overlapping of cropping seasons due to climate change
  4. The impact of subsidies on the over-production of water-intensive crops
Show answer

Answer: The cyclical fluctuation of prices due to time lags between production decisions and harvest

The cobweb model explains price volatility where producers base current production on previous prices, leading to alternating surpluses and shortages.

  1. Only 1 and 2
  2. Only 2 and 3
  3. Only 1 and 3
  4. 1, 2 and 3
Show answer

Answer: Only 2 and 3

Risk is shared; however, the farmer still bears production risks while the buyer manages market risk. Autonomy is often reduced.

Question 243medium

  3. The real value of agricultural exports is increasing

Question 248medium

Which of the following best describes the 'Terms of Trade' (ToT) for the agricultural sector in the context of the Indian economy?

Question 274medium

The Commission for Agricultural Costs and Prices (CACP) recommends MSP based on the weighted average of cost of production. 3. MSP acts as a floor price to protect farmers against sharp falls in agricultural prices.

  1. Only 1 and 2
  2. Only 2 and 3
  3. Only 1 and 3
  4. 1, 2 and 3
Show answer

Answer: Only 2 and 3

MSP is announced only for a specific set of notified crops, not all crops produced in India.

Question 275medium

Which of the following factors most likely leads to 'Agricultural Terms of Trade' (ToT) shifting against the farmers?

  1. Increase in the price of agricultural produce relative to industrial goods
  2. Decrease in the price of industrial inputs relative to agricultural output
  3. Increase in the price of industrial goods relative to agricultural produce
  4. Stable prices for both agricultural and industrial goods
Show answer

Answer: Increase in the price of industrial goods relative to agricultural produce

ToT shifts against farmers when the price of goods they buy (industrial) rises faster than the price of goods they sell (agricultural).

Question 276medium

Consider the following statements regarding the 'PM-KISAN' scheme: 1. It is a Central Sector Scheme providing income support to all landholding farmer families. 2. The funds are transferred directly to the bank accounts of the beneficiaries through DBT. 3. The eligibility is determined by the State Governments.

  1. Only 1 and 2
  2. Only 2 and 3
  3. Only 1 and 3
  4. 1, 2 and 3
Show answer

Answer: 1, 2 and 3

PM-KISAN is a Central Sector Scheme where states identify beneficiaries and funds are transferred via DBT.

Question 277medium

In the context of Indian agriculture, 'Crop Diversification' is primarily intended to achieve which of the following? 1. Reducing the risk of total crop failure due to pests. 2. Improving soil health by breaking monoculture cycles. 3. Reducing the dependence on groundwater for irrigation. 4. Increasing the total area under cereal production.

  1. Only 1 and 2
  2. Only 2 and 3
  3. 1, 2 and 3
  4. 1, 2, 3 and 4
Show answer

Answer: 1, 2 and 3

Crop diversification aims to reduce risk and improve soil health; it typically reduces the dominance of cereals in favor of pulses/oilseeds.

Question 278medium

Which of the following impacts would a significant depreciation of the Indian Rupee have on the agricultural economy?

  1. Decrease in the competitiveness of agricultural exports
  2. Increase in the cost of imported fertilizers and pesticides
  3. Decrease in the domestic price of imported edible oils
  4. Reduction in the incentive for farmers to produce export-oriented crops
Show answer

Answer: Increase in the cost of imported fertilizers and pesticides

Rupee depreciation makes imports (like potash or phosphate) more expensive, increasing the cost of production for farmers.

Question 279medium

Consider the following statements regarding 'Contract Farming' in India: 1. It shifts the production risk from the farmer to the agribusiness firm. 2. It ensures a pre-determined price, reducing price volatility for the farmer. 3. It necessarily eliminates the need for government-mandated MSP.

  1. Only 1 and 2
  2. Only 2 and 3
  3. Only 1 and 3
  4. 1, 2 and 3
Show answer

Answer: Only 1 and 2

Contract farming reduces price risk and production risk; however, it does not legally eliminate the existence of the MSP system.

Question 280medium

The phenomenon of 'Disguised Unemployment' in the Indian agricultural sector is characterized by:

  1. Seasonal unemployment during the non-harvest period
  2. Marginal productivity of labor being zero or negative
  3. Lack of technical skills among the rural workforce
  4. Complete absence of work for the entire year
Show answer

Answer: Marginal productivity of labor being zero or negative

Disguised unemployment occurs when more people are employed than required, meaning their marginal productivity is zero.

Question 285medium

Question 295medium

Which of the following best describes the 'Terms of Trade' (ToT) in the context of the agricultural sector?

  2. The ratio of the price of agricultural exports to the price of agricultural imports.
  3. The difference between the cost of production and the market price of crops.

Show answer

Answer: The ratio of the index of prices received by farmers to the index of prices paid by farmers for non-farm inputs.

Question 297medium

How does an increase in the 'Export Duty' on agricultural commodities typically affect the domestic economy?

  1. It increases domestic prices and encourages higher production.
  2. It decreases domestic prices and discourages exports.
  3. It increases foreign exchange reserves and raises domestic prices.
  4. It has no impact on domestic prices but increases global competitiveness.
Show answer

Answer: It decreases domestic prices and discourages exports.

Export duties make exports costlier, reducing export volume and increasing domestic supply, which lowers domestic prices.

Question 299medium

What is the primary objective of 'Sterilized Intervention' by the RBI when there is a surge in agricultural exports leading to capital inflows?

  1. To increase the domestic inflation rate to discourage imports.
  2. To prevent the appreciation of the Rupee without increasing the domestic money supply.
  3. To decrease the foreign exchange reserves to stabilize the exchange rate.
  4. To encourage farmers to shift from food grains to cash crops.
Show answer

Answer: To prevent the appreciation of the Rupee without increasing the domestic money supply.

Sterilization offsets the increase in money supply resulting from forex purchases to prevent inflation.

Question 301medium

Which of the following factors would lead to a 'Rightward Shift' in the demand curve for an agricultural product?

  1. An increase in the price of a complementary good.
  2. A decrease in the income of consumers in a scenario where the product is an inferior good.
  3. A change in consumer preference favoring the product.
  4. An increase in the price of the agricultural product itself.
Show answer

Answer: A change in consumer preference favoring the product.

A shift in preference increases demand at every price level, shifting the curve to the right.

Question 308medium

Which of the following factors would most likely lead to 'Cost-Push Inflation' in the agricultural sector?

  1. An increase in the demand for organic produce
  2. A sudden hike in the prices of chemical fertilizers and diesel
  3. A bumper harvest leading to a surplus of food grains
  4. An increase in the Minimum Support Price (MSP)
Show answer

Answer: A sudden hike in the prices of chemical fertilizers and diesel

Cost-push inflation occurs when rising input costs (fertilizers, fuel) force producers to raise prices.

Question 310medium

In the context of agricultural economics, what is the 'Cobweb Phenomenon'?

  1. The cyclical fluctuation of prices due to the time lag between production decisions and harvest
  2. The effect of subsidies leading to overproduction of a specific crop
  3. The impact of fragmented land holdings on productivity
  4. The shift from food crops to cash crops due to market signals
Show answer

Answer: The cyclical fluctuation of prices due to the time lag between production decisions and harvest

The Cobweb model explains price volatility where farmers base current production on previous prices, causing supply-demand mismatches.

Question 311medium

  2. To shift the entire risk of crop failure from the farmer to the company

  4. To ensure that only organic crops are grown
Show answer

Answer: To reduce the price volatility for farmers by fixing prices beforehand

Contract farming provides price certainty and reduces market risk by fixing prices before the sowing season.

Question 324medium

If the government increases the procurement price of a crop significantly above the market equilibrium price, what is the most likely economic outcome?

  2. A creation of an agricultural surplus leading to higher government storage costs

Question 329medium

Which of the following best describes the 'Green Revolution's' impact on the Indian economy's structural transformation?

  1. It led to a total shift of labor from agriculture to the service sector
  2. It increased food security but led to regional imbalances and soil degradation
  3. It eliminated the need for government subsidies in agriculture
  4. It decreased the dependency on chemical fertilizers
Show answer

Answer: It increased food security but led to regional imbalances and soil degradation

While it achieved self-sufficiency, it concentrated growth in Punjab/Haryana and caused ecological damage.

Question 330medium

  2. 2 and 3 only
  3. 1 and 3 only
  4. 1, 2 and 3

Answer: 2 and 3 only

  3. The difference between the GDP contribution of agriculture and the manufacturing sector.

Question 334medium

Question 342medium

The phenomenon of 'Cobweb Model' in agricultural economics primarily explains:

  1. The distribution of land holdings among small and marginal farmers
  2. The cyclical fluctuations in prices due to time lags in production decisions
  3. The relationship between irrigation levels and crop yield
  4. The impact of crop rotation on soil fertility
Show answer

Answer: The cyclical fluctuations in prices due to time lags in production decisions

The Cobweb model explains price volatility caused by farmers basing current production on previous prices.

Question 344medium

  3. A bumper harvest of wheat and paddy
  4. A decrease in the interest rates on agricultural loans
Show answer

Answer: A sudden increase in the prices of diesel and fertilizers

Cost-push inflation occurs when the cost of production inputs rises, pushing up the final price of the product.

Question 347medium

In the context of Indian agriculture, what is the primary conceptual difference between 'Agricultural Marketing' and 'Agricultural Trade'?

  1. Marketing involves only transportation, while trade involves only pricing.
  2. Marketing encompasses all activities from harvest to consumption, while trade focuses on the exchange of ownership.
  3. Trade refers to domestic sales, while marketing refers exclusively to exports.
  4. There is no conceptual difference; both terms are used interchangeably in economics.
Show answer

Answer: Marketing encompasses all activities from harvest to consumption, while trade focuses on the exchange of ownership.

Marketing is a broader chain including grading, storage, and distribution, whereas trade is the specific act of buying and selling.

Question 349medium

Which of the following factors would most likely lead to a 'cobweb phenomenon' in the pricing of a specific agricultural commodity?

  1. Perfectly elastic demand and supply curves.
  2. A time lag between the production decision and the actual harvest.
  3. Immediate price adjustment to changes in consumer demand.
  4. Fixed government quotas on production regardless of market price.
Show answer

Answer: A time lag between the production decision and the actual harvest.

The cobweb model occurs when producers base current production on past prices, creating cyclical fluctuations due to time lags.

Question 350medium

How does an increase in the 'Terms of Trade' (ToT) for the agricultural sector typically impact the rural economy?

  1. It decreases the purchasing power of farmers relative to industrial goods.
  2. It indicates that agricultural prices are falling faster than industrial prices.
  3. It increases the real income of farmers by allowing them to buy more industrial goods for the same amount of produce.
  4. It leads to a decrease in the total area under cultivation due to higher profits.
Show answer

Answer: It increases the real income of farmers by allowing them to buy more industrial goods for the same amount of produce.

Higher ToT means the price of agricultural exports/goods rises relative to industrial imports/goods, increasing farmer purchasing power.

Question 351medium

  1. Elimination of market price volatility.
  2. Asymmetry of information and bargaining power favoring the corporate buyer.
  3. Guaranteed minimum price regardless of crop quality.
  4. Reduction in the need for technical inputs.
Show answer

Answer: Asymmetry of information and bargaining power favoring the corporate buyer.

Information asymmetry often leads to unfair contracts where the corporate entity holds more leverage over the small farmer.

Question 384medium

It helps in the integration of agriculture with the industrial value chain. 3. It eliminates the need for the MSP mechanism entirely for the contracted crops.

  1. Only 1
  2. Only 2
  3. Only 1 and 2
  4. 2 and 3
Show answer

Answer: Only 2

Production risk often remains with the farmer; MSP continues to exist as a benchmark regardless of contracts.

Question 385medium

How does a depreciation of the Indian Rupee typically affect India's agricultural trade balance?

  1. It makes agricultural exports cheaper and imports more expensive
  2. It increases the cost of exporting food grains to the global market
  3. It leads to a decrease in the domestic price of imported fertilizers
  4. It has no impact as agricultural trade is conducted in gold
Show answer

Answer: It makes agricultural exports cheaper and imports more expensive

Currency depreciation makes exports more competitive globally and increases the cost of imported agri-inputs.

Question 386medium

Consider the following statements regarding the 'Agriculture Infrastructure Fund' (AIF): 1. It provides medium to long-term debt financing for post-harvest management infrastructure. 2. It is limited only to individual farmers and excludes Farmer Producer Organizations (FPOs). 3. It provides interest subvention to reduce the cost of borrowing.

  1. Only 1
  2. Only 1 and 2
  3. Only 1 and 3
  4. 1, 2 and 3
Show answer

Answer: Only 1 and 3

AIF explicitly includes FPOs, cooperatives, and agri-entrepreneurs, not just individual farmers.

Question 387medium

Which of the following is the primary reason for the 'Paradox of Plenty' (Bumper Crop Paradox) in Indian agriculture?

  1. Increase in the price of crops due to high supply
  2. Fall in market prices during bumper harvests due to inelastic demand
  3. Increase in the cost of storage and warehousing
  4. Decrease in the total production of food grains
Show answer

Answer: Fall in market prices during bumper harvests due to inelastic demand

Inelastic demand means a small increase in supply leads to a large drop in price, reducing total farmer income.

Question 388medium

  1. Commercial banks are not required to lend to agriculture
  2. Agriculture is the only category under PSL
  3. A specific percentage of Adjusted Net Bank Credit must be allocated to agriculture
  4. PSL targets are set by the Ministry of Finance, not the RBI
Show answer

Answer: A specific percentage of Adjusted Net Bank Credit must be allocated to agriculture

RBI mandates that a specific percentage of Adjusted Net Bank Credit (ANBC) must go to the priority sector, including agriculture.

  2. 2 only

  4. Neither 1 nor 2

Answer: Both 1 and 2

CACP recommends MSP based on A2+FL costs, and it acts as a price floor to prevent crashes during surplus production.

Question 400medium

  3. It directly increases the MSP of food grains

Question 402medium

Which of the following combinations describes the 'Green Revolution's' impact on the Indian economy?

  1. Decreased regional disparity and increased crop diversity
  2. Increased food security but increased inter-regional income disparity
  3. Lowered dependence on chemical fertilizers and increased soil health
  4. Decreased the share of agriculture in GDP without increasing productivity
Show answer

Answer: Increased food security but increased inter-regional income disparity

The Green Revolution achieved self-sufficiency in grains but concentrated wealth in Punjab, Haryana, and Western UP.

Question 407medium

  2. The difference between the export and import value of agri-commodities
  3. The ratio of crop yield per hectare to the cost of production
  4. The proportion of agricultural GDP to the total National Income

Answer: The ratio of the price of agricultural goods to the price of industrial goods

Terms of Trade measure the purchasing power of farmers by comparing the prices they receive for crops versus the prices they pay for industrial inputs.

Question 417medium

What is the primary objective of 'Sterilized Intervention' by the RBI in the context of agricultural exports and foreign exchange inflows?

  3. To provide direct subsidies to farmers exporting organic produce.

Sterilization prevents excess liquidity from causing inflation when the RBI buys foreign currency to stabilize the exchange rate.

Question 419medium

Which of the following factors would lead to 'Cost-Push Inflation' specifically within the agricultural sector?

  2. A sudden increase in the global prices of crude oil affecting transport and fertilizer costs.
  3. A bumper harvest of wheat and paddy leading to a supply glut.

Show answer

Answer: A sudden increase in the global prices of crude oil affecting transport and fertilizer costs.

Rising input costs (oil, fertilizers) shift the supply curve, causing cost-push inflation.

Question 423medium

Which of the following factors typically lead to 'Agricultural Terms of Trade' becoming unfavorable for farmers?

Question 433medium

  2. Only 2 and 3
  3. Only 1 and 3
  4. 1, 2 and 3
Show answer

Answer: Only 1 and 2

CACP recommends MSP, but the government announces it. Procurement is not guaranteed for all MSP-notified crops.

Question 440medium

Which of the following factors typically lead to 'Agricultural Terms of Trade' (ToT) shifting in favor of the industrial sector?

  1. Rise in the price of agricultural produce relative to industrial goods
  2. Fall in the price of agricultural produce relative to industrial goods
  3. Stable prices for both agricultural and industrial goods
  4. Increase in government subsidies for agricultural inputs
Show answer

Answer: Fall in the price of agricultural produce relative to industrial goods

Agricultural ToT is the ratio of agricultural prices to industrial prices; a decrease indicates a shift in favor of the industrial sector.

Question 446medium

  4. The lack of skilled labor leads to low agricultural productivity

Answer: More people are engaged in farming than are actually required

Disguised unemployment occurs when the marginal productivity of labor is zero, meaning extra labor adds no additional output.

Question 469medium

Question 493medium

Question 494medium

In the context of Indian agriculture, how does an increase in the 'Loan Waiver' schemes typically impact the agricultural economy in the long run?

  2. It creates a moral hazard, discouraging timely repayment of future loans
  3. It leads to a permanent shift from cereal crops to high-value horticulture
  4. It eliminates the need for crop insurance schemes like PMFBY
Show answer

Answer: It creates a moral hazard, discouraging timely repayment of future loans

Frequent loan waivers create moral hazard, leading to strategic defaults and deteriorating the credit culture in rural banking.

Question 567hard

Question 661hard

Consider the following statements regarding the Minimum Support Price (MSP) and its impact on the Indian economy: 1. An increase in MSP for a specific crop leads to a shift in the production possibility frontier (PPF) of the agricultural sector. 2. MSP acts as a price floor, which can lead to surplus production and increased fiscal burden due to procurement costs. 3. The announcement of MSP primarily aims to curb cost-push inflation in the food sector. Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

  1. 1 and 2 only
  2. 2 only
  3. 2 and 3 only
  4. 1, 2 and 3
Show answer

Answer: 2 only

MSP is a price floor causing surpluses; it does not shift the PPF (which requires resource/tech change) and targets farmer income, not cost-push inflation.

Question 662hard

Regarding the 'Terms of Trade' (ToT) between agriculture and industry in India, which of the following scenarios indicates deteriorating terms of trade for farmers?

  1. The price of agricultural outputs rises faster than the price of industrial inputs.
  2. The price of industrial goods rises faster than the price of agricultural products.
  3. Both agricultural and industrial prices rise at the same rate.
  4. Agricultural prices fall while industrial prices remain constant.
Show answer

Answer: The price of industrial goods rises faster than the price of agricultural products.

Deteriorating ToT occurs when farmers must sell more produce to buy the same amount of industrial goods.

Question 664hard

Which of the following is the most likely consequence of a 'Price Ceiling' imposed by the government on essential food grains during a period of scarcity?

  1. An increase in producer surplus and a reduction in consumer surplus.
  2. The creation of a market surplus and an increase in government procurement.
  3. The emergence of black markets and a shortage of the commodity in the formal market.
  4. A shift in the supply curve to the right, eliminating the scarcity.
Show answer

Answer: The emergence of black markets and a shortage of the commodity in the formal market.

Price ceilings below equilibrium lead to excess demand, resulting in shortages and the growth of illegal black markets.

Question 665hard

In the context of agricultural financing, 'Priority Sector Lending' (PSL) targets are designed to:

  1. Ensure that the RBI can control the inflation rate through direct credit allocation.

  3. Replace the need for institutional credit by promoting informal lending channels.
  4. Eliminate the need for collateral in all agricultural loans regardless of the loan size.
Show answer

Answer: Mandate banks to allocate a specific percentage of Adjusted Net Bank Credit to sectors like agriculture to prevent credit starvation.

PSL ensures credit flows to sectors that might otherwise be neglected by commercial banks due to perceived high risk.

Question 667hard

Which of the following best explains the 'Scissors Crisis' in an agrarian economy?

  1. The simultaneous fall in the price of both agricultural and industrial goods.
  2. The widening gap between the rising prices of industrial goods and the falling prices of agricultural products.
  3. The conflict between small-scale farmers and large-scale corporate farms over land rights.
  4. The fluctuation in crop yields due to the alternating patterns of drought and flood.
Show answer

Answer: The widening gap between the rising prices of industrial goods and the falling prices of agricultural products.

The Scissors Crisis refers to the divergent movement of industrial and agricultural prices, squeezing the farmer's purchasing power.

Question 668hard

  3. A decrease in the price of the commodity in the domestic market.

Show answer

Answer: The imposition of higher import tariffs by the importing countries.

Higher import tariffs increase the price for consumers in the importing country, reducing the quantity demanded at every price level.

Question 673hard

How does a significant depreciation of the Indian Rupee typically impact the economics of Indian agriculture?

  1. It increases the cost of imported fertilizers and pesticides, raising the cost of production.
  2. It reduces the competitiveness of Indian agricultural exports in the global market.
  3. It leads to an immediate decrease in the domestic price of food grains.
  4. It eliminates the incentive for farmers to shift toward high-value export-oriented crops.
Show answer

Answer: It increases the cost of imported fertilizers and pesticides, raising the cost of production.

Rupee depreciation makes imports (like potash/phosphates) more expensive, increasing the cost of inputs for farmers.

Question 674hard

Regarding the 'Price Deficiency Payment' (PDP) model (like Bhavantar Bhugtan Yojana), which of the following is a key conceptual difference from the traditional procurement model?

  1. The government physically procures the produce and stores it in warehouses.
  2. The government pays the difference between the market price and MSP without physical procurement.
  3. The government fixes the market price to ensure it never falls below the MSP.
  4. The model eliminates the need for any price discovery mechanism in the market.
Show answer

Answer: The government pays the difference between the market price and MSP without physical procurement.

PDP provides financial compensation for the price gap without the government needing to handle, store, or transport the produce.

Question 678hard

  2. A fall in ToT increases the real income of farmers, encouraging capital investment in rural areas.
  3. ToT is independent of the inflationary pressures in the industrial sector.

Question 679hard

Consider the impact of 'Sterilized Intervention' by the RBI in the context of agricultural exports. If the RBI buys USD to prevent rupee appreciation, what is the likely indirect effect on the agricultural sector?

  1. It leads to a decrease in the competitiveness of agri-exports due to currency appreciation.
  2. It maintains export competitiveness by preventing the rupee from appreciating, though it may increase domestic liquidity.
  3. It directly increases the MSP of crops by increasing the foreign exchange reserves.
  4. It reduces the inflation rate of food items by restricting the import of essential agri-commodities.
Show answer

Answer: It maintains export competitiveness by preventing the rupee from appreciating, though it may increase domestic liquidity.

Preventing rupee appreciation keeps exports cheaper for foreign buyers, supporting agri-exporters, while sterilization manages the resulting liquidity.

Question 680hard

Which of the following best describes the 'Cobweb Phenomenon' in the context of Indian agricultural price volatility?

  1. The tendency of crop prices to remain stagnant despite changes in demand.
  2. The lag between the production decision and the actual harvest, leading to cyclical price fluctuations.
  3. The impact of government subsidies on the overproduction of water-intensive crops.
  4. The correlation between global commodity price crashes and domestic farm distress.
Show answer

Answer: The lag between the production decision and the actual harvest, leading to cyclical price fluctuations.

The Cobweb model explains price volatility caused by producers basing current production on previous period's prices.

Question 682hard

Question 685hard
